The Level of Care Assessment process flow described below is very similar to that for Katie Beckett. While an LTSS client does not require a MART review, they will need to have a Level of Care Assessment determined. Sherlock and SSI Medicaid clients who request LTSS will also have to meet the Level of Care Assessment criteria to receive LTSS benefits.  A task will be generated for the LTSS Unit 90 days prior to the renewal date of the Level of Care.  The system will not take any automatic action on the LTSS case even if the Level of Care Assessment has expired. 

Below is the Level of Care Process flow which is similar to that for Katie Beckett - 




LTSS Medicaid ? Group Composition

A client is considered to be applying for Medicaid-funded LTSS in the HCBS or institutional-setting, if they meet the following conditions:
* Has completed a DHS-2 application and
* Indicates that they need assistance in performing daily activities in the Special Circumstances screen in the MAGI flow and
* Is over the age of 18 (except for SSI ? LTSS where there is no minimum age limit) and 
* Has a Level of Care in a Pending Status
Only the LTSS applicant is considered in the LTSS EDG in determining their eligibility for LTSS.  Their community partner, dependents and dependents of the community partner will be included as ?excluded? members of the EDG. As part of the post-eligibility financial determination, the LTSS applicant?s community partner and dependents will be included in determining their cost of care.  If the community partner is on LTSS Medicaid or SSI Medicaid then their income and resources are not considered.

For MAGI LTSS applicant is considered in the LTSS EDG in determining their eligibility for MAGI LTSS. Their community partner, dependents and dependents of the community partner will be included as ?Filing? unit members of the EDG. During Resource Eligibility only applicant?s resources are considered. They are eligible for CSRS deductions towards their resource countable value. 

The LTSS EDG group is created when the user submits a DHS-2 application and runs eligibility determination.  If the client is potentially LTSS-eligible, an LTSS ? Pending case is created when the case is in Intake mode.  An LTSS-Pending case can be created in the Case Change mode if a new Level of Care is initiated after the initial eligibility determination. 

Following are the variants of LTSS Medicaid with some additional criteria that is required for building their group composition:
> SSI with LTSS
> Special Income (in addition to above group composition criteria, individual indicates that they are aged, blind or disabled).
> HCBS Waiver (in addition to above group composition criteria, individual indicates that they are aged, blind or disabled).
> Medically Needy (in addition to above group composition criteria, individual indicates that they are aged, blind or disabled).
> MAGI Expansion 

A person is evaluated for LTSS ? Special Income if 
1. They have a Nursing Home or Hospital LOC and 
2. They have Highest or Hospital Care Level and
3. They are in an Institutional program type or Unknown (no) program type.  
In this situation, they would be living in a facility like a nursing home, hospital, private psychiatric hospital etc. They cannot be in multiple facilities at the same time. When a person moves from Institutional program to a non-institutional program, the TOA for the person will change from LTSS ? Special Income to LTSS ? HCBS (as long as they meet other criteria). 

If a person is in the 217 ? HCBS Waiver TOA, they need to have ? 
1. Any assessment type (except Katie Beckett) and
2. Highest, High, Hospital or Preventive Care Level and
3. Program type that is not institutional.
In this situation, the user could be living in an Assisted Living facility, Group Home, PACE, Hab Waiver etc.  The user is able to enter multiple Plans of Care (non-overlapping) to record the client?s movements between programs. Within one plan of care, if the client is in the community, a client can receive multiple community services at the same time. 


Their Financial pathway is discussed in detail in the below section.

LTSS Medicaid ? Non-Financial
Applicants are expected to meet the following non-financial characteristics in order to be determined eligible for LTSS Medicaid: 

* Must be a resident of Rhode Island
* Must be a citizen of the United States or a Lawfully Present Non-Citizen
* Must not be incarcerated
* Must provide a valid SSN
* Must report access to public or non-public MEC
* Must have a level of care determination
Note: LTSS clients are not subject to a MART disability determination process. 

 
LTSS Medicaid ? Financial
Only the LTSS client?s income and resources are used for the initial determination of financial eligibility.  During Resource eligibility, community spouse resource allowance is deducted from the total countable asset value. 

Following are the Eligibility path ways for LTSS Medicaid clients.

MAGI ? LTSS eligibility:  For a client to be considered MAGI ? LTSS (Cat Elig or Med Needy), they will need to meet the MAGI income criteria. When evaluated for resources, they will need to meet the LTSS resources criteria. 

SSI ? LTSS  eligibility: For a client to be considered SSI ? LTSS eligible, they will need to meet the SSI income limits. This is determined by the Social Security Administration. Once they are approved as SSI-eligible, they will only be evaluated based on the LTSS resource criteria to be evaluated for SSI ? LTSS eligibility. 

At the point of application, the following incomes are considered as part of the income calculation for an individual ? 
* Earned Income
* Self-Employment Income
* Title II (Social Security Benefits)
* Rental Income
* Other Unearned Income

The following resources are considered as part of the resource calculation for an individual ? 
* Liquid
* Burial
* Vehicle
* Real Property
* Life Insurance
* Trust
* Lump sum
Post-Eligibility Cost of Care:

?Cost of care calculations will be done only if the Level of Care Services are authorized. If the services are not authorized then cost of care calculation is not done by the system. It will display as $0.00. This information is not sent to MMIS.?

All LTSS clients are responsible for a patient share portion for their cost of care. This monthly cost of care is calculated as part of the post-eligibility process. In the determination of patient share, the following people will be considered as part of the group composition ? 
* LTSS applicant
* Community spouse
* LTSS applicant?s dependents
* Community spouse?s dependents
In determining the patient share amount, the income and resources are taken into account, with certain allowable deductions and disregards. The remaining income will then be used to determine the patient share. 

The allowable income deductions in calculating the cost of care are ? 

1. Personal Needs Deduction or $90 Reduced Pension Deductions
2. Community Spouse Allowance
3. Community Dependent Allowance
4. Medical Insurance Premiums
5. Medical/Remedial Items
6. Home Maintenance Deductions
7. First/Last Month Institutional Expenses

There are no expected changes in the verifications process for LTSS Medicaid. If a client also applies for LTSS, they will be subject to LTSS verifications process, where applicable.  Detailed specifications of the verifications process is outlined in 03 18-P2-Process Doc-Eligibility-Automation of Verification for Complex Medicaid.

LTSS Medicaid ? Renewals
LTSS cases will be renewed annually. The LTSS worker will have to manually renew the Level of Care Assessment. Details for the renewal process can be found in the 03.19-P2-ProcessDoc-Eligibility-Passive Renewal.

LTSS Medicaid ? Screens and Tables
The LTSS Unit will have access to initiate and edit the Level of Care Assessment screens. The Level of Care screens are included in the Design Artifacts Inserted Section of this document. The new tables developed to capture the Level of Care information is also included in the Design Artifacts Inserted Section of this document. 

Once eligibility determination is run, LTSS Medicaid will also display the following post-eligibility screens.  The post-eligibility screens are included in the Design Artifacts Inserted section of this document. 

LTSS Medicaid ? Tasks/Alerts/Mass Updates
* For a new DHS-2 Medicaid application, after eligibility determination for MAGI programs, if the client is determined potentially eligible for LTSS Medicaid, a task is created to the LTSS Unit to evaluate the case. 
* A task is created to the SSI Unit to close a SSI eligibility when the Level of Care is authorized and eligibility is run again. 
* A task is created to the LTSS Unit 90 days before an authorized Level of Care Assessment is due to expire. **Please note that no action will be taken on an LTSS case even if the Level of Care Assessment is past due.**
* LTSS will be part of regular Medicaid case instead of separate case. When LTSS worker runs eligibility system will determine eligibility only for Medicaid and MPP program. If the same case has other public assistance programs a task will be generated to change queue to review information updated and determine eligibility public assistance programs.

LTSS Medicaid ? Security
* The LTSS Unit will have read-write access to the Level of Care screens. 
* The LTSS Unit will have the security to clear LTSS tasks. 
* Access to the Level of Care screens for other users is defined in the Level of Care section. 
* LTSS will be part of regular Medicaid case instead of separate case. When LTSS worker runs eligibility system will allow LTSS Unit to Approve/Certify only for Medicaid and MPP program. If the same case has other public assistance programs a task will be generated to change queue to review information updated and determine eligibility public assistance programs.

LTSS Medicaid ? Batches/Interfaces
The following batches/interfaces will be impacted by this change:
MMIS Interface
The MMIS interface will include information on Level of Care Assessment and Plan of Care Services being sent to MMIS. There are three transaction files impacted by the Level of Care and Plan of Care Services. They are ? 
1. E Transaction - The Level of Care information will be included as part of the E transaction. 
2. G Transaction - The Waiver Code and Plan of Care information will be included as part of the existing G transaction. In addition to this, the 1G transaction will contain a new Acuity Level field that will be send to MMIS. 
3. U Transaction ? This is a new transaction that will include details for all authorized services for a plan of care. The U transaction is triggered when there is an addition or modification to specific Plan of Care Services only. 

1E Transaction: 

An MMIS ?1E? transaction is triggered when a Level of Care Assessment is authorized and at least one of the institutional program has been authorized.

When the Level of Care Assessment end date has expired, it is expected that worker will update level of care assessment and reevaluate eligibility. RIBridges will trigger a new transaction being sent upon the renewal of the level of care assessment. If a Level of Care Assessment does not have an End Date, the LOC Assessment will remain open until the user changes it in RIBridges.

U Transactions:
RIBRIDGES sends out 1U Transaction only when services are authorized or an authorized service is modified for LTSS Community Programs. It is triggered ONLY when the Prior Authorization Status for the particular service is ?Authorized?. If the Prior Authorization Status ?Not Required? or blank, the service is not sent to MMIS through the 1U transaction. It is possible for an individual to have multiple services authorized for the same duration. The 1U transaction is applicable only to certain, pre-defined service types and the system will translate the Service Type and Frequency to determine the Procedure code to be sent to MMIS.  The 1U transaction is triggered from both Data Collection screens as well as when there is a change to the Plan of Care Services from the main Menu bar through the ?Others? navigation. In this instance, the trigger is created through the Plan of Care ? Details/Services screen and the user does not have to run eligibility to re-determine eligibility or to send the 1U transaction to MMIS.

Additionally, the system sends out 3U and 4U Transactions for cancellation and Terminations of LTSS Community Program services.

Batch ? LOC Renewal
This batch will be used to create tasks for case workers when the level of care assessment is due for renewal. 

Batch Logic: 
1. Gather all the cases that have an approved Level of Care determination within 90 days of the batch run. 
2. Verify that there is no existing level of care determination with a begin date greater than the selected level of care end date for the same client. 
3. If the case is an LTSS case, create a task for the LTSS Unit worker for Level of Care renewal.  The alert text should state ?Level of Care determination for case due for renewal. Please review case and take the necessary action.?
4. If the case is a Katie Beckett case, and the level of care determination is due for renewal, create a task for the Katie Beckett Unit worker. The alert text should state ?Level of Care determination for case due for renewal. Please review case and take the necessary action.?
5. At the end of the batch, create a log file to report the successful run of the batch. 
6. End of batch. 

LTSS Medicaid ? Notices
There are no expected changes to the Notices based on this type of assistance.

3.11 Community Medicaid (ABD)
Community Medicaid ? Group Composition
Community Medicaid is determined if the client is residing in Community and Aged/Disabled.
A client is considered to be applying for Community Medicaid if they meet the following conditions:
* Has completed a DHS-2 application and
* Is above or equal to the age of 65 or 
* Indicates that they have a disability and
* Has a MART review pending or approved for SSI or RSDI Disability benefits.
o Or have one of the following SSI denial reasons:
* Lose SSI due to Title II-D benefits (DAC-eligible)
* Lose SSI due to Widow(er) RSDI Survivor Entitlement (Disabled Widower Eligible)
* Lose SSI due to RSDI COLA increase (Pickle eligible)
* Lose SSI due to SSI Actuarial Changes (SSI Act-Change eligible)
* Lose SSI due to Protected Widow(er) benefits (Protected Widower eligible)
While determining Medicaid group composition, client?s group budgeting includes only the client and community partner. Community partner?s resources are used in resource eligibility. Community partner?s income is used income eligibility.

Hierarchy of program evaluation is, as follows:
? AB - Blind: Deeming rules are applied for ABD - Blind. If there is a spouse then family size of 2 is used.  A person is eligible for AB ? Blind if they are identified with a disability of ?Blind?.  This is the primary non-financial criteria for a person to be eligible for this TOA.  They will need to meet the Cat Needy Limits as part of their financial criteria. 
? AD - Low Income: Deeming rules are applied for Low Income. Deeming rules are not applied if there is a spouse then family size of 2 is used. A person is eligible for AD ? Low Income if they are aged or disabled and their disability is other than blindness. They need to meet the SSI Income Limits (100% FPL) as part of their financial criteria.
? ABD - Medically needy: Deeming rules are applied for Medically Needy. 
? Flex: Whenever Medically Needy is denied due to excess income and Resource eligibility requirements are met.


Community programs follow the deeming rules:
If there is ineligible spouse or ineligible parent then deeming rules are used. 
The definition of ?ineligible? is as following. If the member meets all of the following conditions then they are considered as ?ineligible? individual for Community program.
1. All of the following conditions should meet 
a. Client is not requesting for Medicaid.
b. If the client is not eligible for SSI
c. If the client is not eligible for RIW
If the Assistance Unit member is ?ineligible spouse/parent?, 
1. If there is income to be deemed then Family size of 2 to be applied in income calculation. 
2. If there is resource to be deemed then Family size of 2 to be applied in resource calculation. 
3. If there is no income or resources to be deemed and the member is requesting Medicaid then family size of 2 to be applied in income or resource calculation. 
4. If there is no income or resources to be deemed and the member is not requesting Medicaid or then family size of 1 to be applied in income or resource calculation.
If the both the spouses/parent are determined MPP eligible then their income is NOT deemed. They are counted together and tested against the Family size of 2.
Community Medicaid ? Non-Financial
Following are the non-financial characteristics Community Medicaid clients are required to meet in order to be determined eligible for Community Medicaid.
* Name
* Date of Birth
* SSN/Enumeration
* Citizenship
* Immigration
* Incarceration
* Resident of Rhode Island 
* Third Party Liability i.e., Access to Non-Public MEC or Public MEC
* Disability requirements through a MART review or through SSI/RSDI ? Disability determination if the client is under 65 years of age.

Community Medicaid ? Financial
There are no changes to financial requirements for Community Medicaid as part of these changes. 

Community Medicaid ? Verifications
The following data points will be verified for Community Medicaid as part of the eligibility verifications process ? 

Data Point(s)Verified for the Type of Assistance?NameYesDate of BirthYesSSNYesCitizenshipYesImmigration StatusYesImmigration ? 5 Year Bar MetYesIncarceration StatusYesDeceased IndicatorYesCurrent Income (Title II)YesCurrent Income (Wages)YesESI MECNoNon-Employer Sponsored Insurance (ESI) Minimum Essential Coverage (MEC)NoUnearned IncomeYesSelf-Employment IncomeYesResourcesYes
If all the data points for an applicant are verified through external data sources, they are automatically authorized for Community Medicaid.  The worker does not have to do a manual authorization of this case.

There is no post-eligibility verification for Community Medicaid. 

Community Medicaid ? Renewals
Community Medicaid cases will come for renewal twelve (12) months after it is approved. Flex Programs are due by six (6) months. At the end of the six (6) months system shall close their Medicaid (Flex) ineligibility. Client needs to resubmit new Medicaid application for Flex clients. 

Community Medicaid ? Screens and Tables
There are no screens or tables impacted with Community Medicaid. 

Community Medicaid ? Tasks/Alerts/Mass Updates
* Whenever MART documents are received in the local office a Task is generated to MART Unit. 
* Whenever MART is due for renewal before 90 days from renewal date system will create a task to the local DHS Unit to have the appropriate forms mailed to the client. 
* Whenever MART form is not received from the client within 45 days from the form sent date, then system shall run eligibility through mass update and close Community Medicaid.
* Mass update is triggered at the sixth month for Flex clients to close flex eligibility.

3.12 Sherlock Plan
Specifications for this Type of Assistance are detailed in the 03.20-P2-Process Doc-Eligibility-Sherlock Changes.

3.13 Medicare Premium Payment
MPP program is approved only if the client is enrolled or entitled to Part A and/or Part B Medicare programs. Hierarchy of program evaluation is as follows:
* Qualified Medicare Beneficiary (QMB)
* Specified Low Income  Medicare Beneficiaries (SLMB)
* Qualified Individuals (QI-1)
MPP programs follow the deeming rules:
If there is ineligible spouse or ineligible parent then deeming rules are used. 
The definition of ?ineligible? is as following. If the member meets all of the following conditions then they are considered as ?ineligible? individual for MPP program.
2. All of the following conditions should meet 
a. Client is	 not requesting for MPP assistance or Medicaid.
b. If the client is not eligible for SSI
c. If the client is not eligible for RIW
If the Assistance Unit member is ?ineligible spouse/parent?, 
5. If there is income to be deemed then Family size of 2 to be applied in income calculation. 
6. If there is resource to be deemed then Family size of 2 to be applied in resource calculation. I
7. If there is no income or resources to be deemed and the member is requesting Medicaid or MPP then family size of 2 to be applied in income or resource calculation. 
8. If there is no income or resources to be deemed and the member is not requesting Medicaid or MPP then family size of 1 to be applied in income or resource calculation.
If the both the spouses/parent are determined MPP eligible then their income is NOT deemed. They are counted together and tested against the Family size of 2.
Note: If the spouse/parent is Long Term Care client or Community/HCBS client then there is no deeming of their income and resources towards the eligible spouse/child.
* QMB Eligibility is determined from the next month of application date. For new applications, for the month of application, we should not be cascading down the eligibility to SLMB to QI-1 if their income is under 100% FPL. Retro Medicaid coverage cannot be requested for QMB. 
* SLMB Eligibility is determined from the application month. Retro Medicaid coverage can be requested for SLMB. 
* QI-1 Eligibility is determined from the application month, however if the application date is prior to calendar year then eligibility is determined from the Calendar year begin date. Client who is not eligible for Medicaid is evaluated for QI-1. If the client is determined Medicaid eligible, then they are not eligible for QI-1.
For example: if the application date is 12/02/2014 and eligibility is determined on 01/15/2014 then individual is determined eligible only from 01/01/2014. 
Retro Medicaid coverage can be requested for QI-1. However it can be requested only within a calendar year. If the application date is 02/02/2014 then Retro coverage can be requested only from 01/01/2014.
During Eligibility determination, if the client is not eligible for QMB because their application month is denied due to the reason that they cannot receive QMB for application month. However, they meet all the criteria?s of QMB eligibility then, system should not cascade down to SLMB or QI-1. It should not show any records for application month. 
Note: SSI clients will have their QMB approved in SSI case, if they meet the QMB criteria.
Individuals and spouses income and resources are considered during group composition.

3.14 DCYF Medicaid
DCYF administrates five different kinds of Medicaid.   Namely,
* Adoption Subsidy with Title IV-E
* Adoption Subsidy without Title IV-E
* Foster Care with Title IV-E
* Foster Care without Title IV-E
* State Adoption Subsidy
* MA - Chafee
Whenever application type is selected as ?DCYF Medicaid? in program request screen then system shall evaluate for following categories of assistance.
Adoption Subsidy with Title IV-E
This coverage group include the adopted children under 18, who are eligible for Title IV-E adoption subsidy program.  Child becomes ineligible under the following circumstances.
* Child is aged out.
* Child is removed from DCYF Adoption Subsidy program.
* Child is deceased.
* Child is moved out of the state.
Foster Care with Title IV-E
This coverage group include the foster children under 21, who are eligible for Title IV-E for foster care maintenance program. 
Adoption Subsidy without Title IV-E
This coverage group include the adopted children under 21, who are eligible for department ward adoption subsidy program.  Child becomes ineligible under the following circumstances.
* Child is aged out.
* Child is removed from DCYF Adoption Subsidy program.
* Child is deceased.
* Child is moved out of the state.
Foster Care without Title IV-E
This coverage group includes foster children under 21 who are eligible for department ward for foster care maintenance program. 
State Adoption Subsidy
This coverage group is for children between the age of 18 and 21 who have been adopted and not eligible for federal subsidies.
Other Rules
There is no Financial or Verification requirement for DCYF Medicaid. The system will generate notices when a case is approved or closed in RIBridges.  These are Shell cases to issue Medical Benefits for DCYF children.
3.15 Creation of Duplicate Accounts
The system currently does not allow individuals to get health insurance coverage simultaneously across two different accounts/cases. This ensures that an individual does not get double-coverage of subsidized health insurance. However, there are some situations where individuals should be allowed to have active coverage across two separate cases. This is particularly true when a parent is court-ordered to provide unsubsidized coverage for a child who has subsidized health insurance in another case. Similarly, the system currently does not will allow an individual active on a SHOP account through the Exchange to apply for benefits through an independent individual account simultaneously.  
In order for the system to ensure that a client receives sufficient but not duplicate coverage, the system will have to make the following changes ? 
1. The customer portal will need to allow for an individual to exist in multiple active accounts across account types, as detailed below.
2. The worker portal will need to allow an admin user to override the restriction for a client to get health coverage across two individual accounts. 
3. Eligibility will need to ensure that a person does not have subsidized health coverage simultaneously across two separate accounts/cases. 
4. Eligibility will need to allow for a person to have subsidized and unsubsidized health coverage simultaneously across two separate accounts/cases. 

Screen Edits across Customer and Worker Portal

1. Customer Portal ? 
In the customer portal, the ?You and Your Family Members? page currently has an edit that prevents users from creating and being active in multiple accounts based on their SSN. If a user tries to add someone who already exists in the system with the same SSN, the client gets an edit stating that the person with the same SSN already receives benefits. This prevents the client from adding this person to the second account. 

This edit needs to be relaxed under certain circumstances. The types of accounts where a client can exist in more than one account are ? 
SHOP AccountIndividual AccountBroker AccountNavigator AccountSHOP AccountNOT ALLOWEDALLOWEDALLOWEDALLOWEDIndividual AccountALLOWEDNOT ALLOWEDALLOWEDALLOWEDBROKER AccountALLOWEDALLOWEDNOT ALLOWEDALLOWEDNavigator AccountALLOWEDALLOWEDALLOWEDNOT ALLOWED
In other words, a person cannot be active in two SHOP accounts, or two individual accounts etc. In these circumstances, the screen will throw an edit stating that the person already exists. However, if a person in a SHOP account attempts to be included in an individual account, the system will not prevent them from being active recipients in two separate accounts. Similarly, in the worker portal, the system will not prevent a user from being added in the Program Request screen. 

If a user tries to create an account in one of the ?Not Allowed? conditions, the system will display an error message for a duplicate account. 


Modification in Eligibility Determination:

Currently, eligibility rules ensure that a person does not get coverage for the same program across multiple accounts/cases for the same period of time. This ensures that the person does not get duplicate coverage across accounts. This rule will continue in effect for all programs, including private insurance. A person cannot get overlapping coverage for subsidized private insurance or Medicaid across accounts/cases. 

A client can get duplicate coverage across accounts/cases simultaneously under very specific scenarios.  If the client can request for coverage across two independent accounts (getting through the screen edits which allows a client to request coverage only in certain circumstances), eligibility will further ensure that they do not get duplicate coverage. The only circumstance in which they get duplicate coverage is if they are applying for health insurance in one account and unsubsidized health insurance in the second account. To do this, they would have not selected the ?Requesting Financial Assistance? checkbox in the Program Request screen. This implies that they client requests unsubsidized health coverage. Similarly, if they exist in one account with unsubsidized health coverage, they can be found eligible for Medicaid or subsidized QHP in the other account.

The table below illustrates the type of medical insurance an individual can be eligible for across two different accounts. 

Medicaid(MAGI and Complex)Subsidized QHPUnsubsidized QHPMedicaid(MAGI and Complex)NOT ALLOWEDNOT ALLOWEDALLOWEDSubsidized QHPNOT ALLOWEDNOT ALLOWEDALLOWEDUnsubsidized QHPALLOWEDALLOWEDALLOWED

When the user runs eligibility, the system will have an edit to check for the combination of coverage across multiple accounts. If the client has Medicaid in the first account and are eligible for Medicaid for subsidized QHP in the second account as well, they will be denied benefits with the notice text as ?Individual is already receiving health coverage in another account.?

If the client has Medicaid or subsidized QHP in the first account, they will be allowed to receive unsubsidized QHP in the second account. Similarly, if the client has unsubsidized QHP in the first account, they will be allowed to receive subsidized QHO or Medicaid in the second account. 


3.16 Other Miscellaneous Changes
The following changes need to be made in order to accommodate additional requirements reqarding processing eligibility in RIBridges. 
Task Generation Functionality
The system will allow and accommodate for workers identified as requiring further supervision. These workers will not be able to authorize any eligibility unless there is second party/supervisory review.  The workers are identified as needing second party review in their user profiles. Based on this identification, they will be able to run eligibility in a case but will not be able to authorize the eligibility. Once supervisory approval has been received, the users will be able to authorize eligibility. 
The Eligibility process will use the flag in the worker profile to identify if the Authorize button on the Finalize Eligibility screen will be displayed. If the worker is identified as requiring second party review, the eligibility process will display or not display the Authorize button. 

Partial Authorization/Disposition
The system will enforce the partial disposition of cases based on the user profile and security profile of the logged in user.  The following conditions are enforced to ensure that specialized cases are authorized only by particular units ? 
b. An LTSS program can be authorized only by a user identified as belonging to the LTC unit. This is based on their security profile identified. If a case has both LTSS and a DHS program or a non-LTSS health insurance, the LTSS Unit will be able to authorize only the LTSS eligibility. The other programs will not be authorized by the LTSS unit. 
c. A Katie Becket program can be authorized only by a user identified as belonging to the Katie Beckett unit. This is based on their identified security profile. If a case has both Katie Beckett and another DHS program or a non-Katie Beckett health insurance, the Katie Beckett worker can authorize only the Katie Beckett eligibility. 
d. Contact Center workers will be identified by their security profiles. Users belonging to this security profile can authorize only MAGI and private health insurance. They will not be able to authorize other DHS programs. 
e. Eligibility Technicians will be able to authorize all programs except for LTSS and Katie Beckett. 
Excluding Specified Individuals from Medicaid
The system will prevent or close eligibility of certain ?banned? individuals from receiving Medicaid. In certain situations, CMS notifies the agency of individuals who have been committing Medicaid fraud and should be banned from receiving Medicaid during the timeframe that they are banned.  The Admin will be able to use the Fraud Request screens in RIBridges to indicate that the person has committed fraud. The Sanction Start and End Dates indicate the period of time that the individual is banned from being eligible for Medicaid. The updated eligibility information is sent to MMIS accordingly.

If the person has existing Medicaid eligibility, the Admin will use the Eligibility Override functionality to close the individual?s eligibility. This will override the system-calculated eligibility and the client will be closed. The system will trigger the CNE and Medicaid Termination Notices. The individual can be evaluated for QHP/APTC/CSR eligibility.  When the eligibility for the individual is re-run, the rules will consider that this individual is ?banned? from Medicaid and deny Medicaid until the sanction end date, if applicable. 

If CMS provides the agency with a client who is not currently receiving or enrolled in Medicaid, the system will allow the  user to create the individual in the system. If the client were to apply for Medicaid, they should not be eligible for Medicaid based on the indicator that they are banned from Medicaid for fraud. 

Adverse Action for Medicaid Termination ? if an individual is identified for fraud, the individual is given 15 days for adverse action prior to their Medicaid termination date. 
* If the fraud is reported before the 15th of the month, the Medicaid eligibility is terminated as of the end of the month. 
o For example if the Sanction Start Date is November 13th, the Medicaid eligibility is terminated as of November 30th. 
* If the fraud is reported after the 15th of the month, the Medicaid eligibility is terminated as of the end of the following month, giving them 15 days of adverse action. 
o For example, if the Sanction Start Date is November 15th, the Medicaid eligibility is terminated as of December 31st. 
* If an excluded person has their sanction reversed, they would now have a Sanction End Date on their Fraud Request record. If the Sanction End Date is prior to the 15th of the month, they can be Medicaid eligible as of the 1st of the same month. 
o For example, if the Sanction End Date is identified as November 13th, they can be made Medicaid Eligible as of November 1st. 
* If the person has a Sanction End Date on the 15th or later, the person will be Medicaid eligible as of the 1st of the next month. 
o For example, if the Sanction End Date is identified as November 15th they can be Medicaid eligible as of December 1st. 

The screens for identifying the individuals banned from being eligible for Medicaid will be recorded in the 05 11 02_SF_FM_FMCBR_CreateFraudBenefitRequest. 

Below is the process flow for identifying and processing who should be excluded from Medicaid ? 





3.17 Design Artifacts Inserted (otherwise refer to attachment)

Please note that wireframes contained in this document may be subject to change as a result of text updates that were made associated with Deloitte?s response to the State?s comments.
02.03.10: Level of Care Summary
The Level of Care Summary screen is accessed from the Non-Financial flow of the DHS-2 application. It is enabled only if the client indicates that they need long-term support and services in the Special Circumstances screen.  The Level of Care Summary screen provides an overview of the level of care details that have been entered. It also allows the user to access the Level of Care ?Details screen.  When the user initially accesses the Level of Care ? Summary screen, they will not see any data. Clicking the Add button on this screen will open the Level of Care Details screen for the user. 




























02.03.10: Wireframe

 
Please refer to Widget 02.03.10 for more details on this screen.
Level of Care Details
This screen allows the user to initiate, approve and deny a Level of Care Assessment. It also allows the user to identify the Care Level that has been authorized, the dates of care and other details regarding their level of care.  The Level of Care Details screen is enabled when the user clicks ?Add? on the Level of Care ? Summary screen.  














02.03.09: Wireframe


Please refer to Widget 02.03.09_DC_Level of Care Details for more details on this screen.

Plan of Care Summary

The Plan of Care Summary screen is accessed when a Level of Care is Approved on the Details screen. It can be accessed if the user clicks Add (if the Plan of Care has not been initiated) or if the user clicks Next (if there is an existing Plan of Care).  The Plan of Care Summary screen provides summary information on the Plans of Care associated with the particular level of care.  It will lead to the Plan of Care Details screen. 

02.03.12: Wireframe


Please refer to Widget 02.03.12_DC_Plan_Of_Care_Summary for more details on this screen.


Plan of Care Details

The Plan of Care Details screen is used to capture information on the particular Plan of Care authorized at the Level of Care. It also captures the facilities or services the client is authorized for based on their clinical and functional evaluation. The Plan of Care Details screen is enabled when the Level of Care Assessment Status is ?Approved?. 

The user will be able to enter a Plan of Care without specifying a facility or services. They will be able to come at a later point and add new or modify existing facilities or services. If the ?Program Type? defined is ?Community?, the user will be able to provide multiple details in the Services section. The fields displayed in the table are dynamically changed to reflect service-specific fields. If the Program Type is defined as ?Institutional?, the user will be able to provide facility-related information for the client.  The user will be able to add multiple Plans of Care in order to reflect both Institutional and HCBS services provided. The wireframes below display the fields as they will appear for a ?Community? program type and an ?institutional? program type. 




02.03.11: Wireframe

 








Please refer to Widget 02.03.11_DC_Plan_Of_Care_Details for more details on this screen.

Filing Unit Summary
This screen is displayed when the post-eligibility under the following circumstances:  
1. When a DHS-2 application has been submitted and an LTSS case has been built.
2. Whenever the user uses the ?Eligibility Search? functionality to view the eligibility results of a case. 
The user should have an LTSS case in one of the following statuses for any of the LTSS TOAs: 
1. Client has an LTSS ? Pending Case
2. Client has an LTSS ? Approved Case
3. Client has an LTSS ? Denied Case

3.18 Interfaces ? MMIS
As part of MMIS Eligibility Transaction, a new transaction called as ?2B? is added in addition to existing ?1B? ,?3B? and ?4B? transaction.
2B Transaction is used to send the historic (retro Medicaid) coverage to MMIS system, whenever the client doesn?t have eligibility for the historic period. Expectation is to have the Eligibility Begin Date and End Date in the past period as part of the 2B Transaction.
Scenario 1: Client is applying for Medicaid with Application date of 04/10/2015 and determined eligible on 04/10/2015. 1B Transaction is sent to MMIS with Eligibility Start Date as 04/01/2015. Later on client continued to apply for Retro coverage for prior month?s i.e, Jan 2015, Feb 2015 and March 2015 through DHS-2 application/Health Insurance application. Worker processed the retro coverage on 04/20/2015. In this case only Retro Months (01/2015,02/2015,03/2015) should be sent as ?2B? to MMIS.  

Day#Transaction#Elig Start DateStop DateAid Category CodeDescriptionTransaction04/10/201514/1/2015CXChildless Adult Medicaid1B04/20/201511/1/20153/31/2015MA2B
Scenario 2: Client is applying for MAGI and determined eligible. However requested Retro coverage. Worker is processing retro coverage on same day. In this scenario only Retro Months should be sent as 2B along 1B to MMIS. The HP enrollment system (MMIS) will accept two ?B? transactions on same day as long as one of the transaction is ongoing with no end date whereas the other retro has start and end dates which do not overlap with the ongoing transaction. Application date here is some date in 3rd month hence MAGI starts prospectively from 1st of 4th month.

Day#Transaction#Elig Start DateStop DateAid Category CodeDescriptionTransaction111/1/20153/31/2015MA2B124/1/2015CX1B
Scenario 3: Client is eligible for MAGI Medicaid on the current month which is 3rd month. The dependent children are aging out. Hence the parents move to CX effective next (4th month) month. That means LIF aid category code for the parents closes end of the month in which dependents age out. 

Day#Transaction#Elig Start DateStop DateAid Category CodeDescriptionTransaction113/1/20153/31/2015UFLow Income Families2B124/1/2015CXChildless Adult Medicaid1B

Scenario 4: Client is currently eligible for MAGI Medicaid as CHIP effective 07/1/2014. Client has reported a change as well as aging out of the system effective 08/01/2015. In this scenario New Aid Category should be set prospectively.

Day#Transaction#Elig Start DateStop DateAid Category CodeDescriptionTransaction116/1/20157/31/2015UJCHIP2B128/1/2015CXChildless Adult Medicaid1B

As part of MMIS Demographics (?1A00? ? Transaction) following are the additional fields added to the existing story boards.
f. US Entry Date: Date Non-Citizen entered US. This is used by MMIS to consider these individuals as Refugee, if the recipient entered U.S in the last eight (8) months. 
g. Email Address: Email address of the recipient or primary applicant.
Field NameFormatPositionDescriptionEmail AddressAlphanumeric232-281Email address of the applicant. This field can be blank. US Entry DateNumeric282-289US Entry Date in CCYYMMDD format. If this is not applicable, the system will send the date as 00/00/0000.

3.19 Business Rules Listings
The following section describes the OPA rules used for evaluating an applicant?s Medicaid eligibility. This includes the rules that drives the evaluation of a person?s MAGI eligibility, complex Medicaid eligibility and private insurance eligibility, based on the cascading logic of the Medicaid Hierarchy. 
Group Composition
the person (the other person) is a member of the person's tax household members if
any
all
the person is a tax filer
the person is not claimed as a dependent
either
			  the next person is claimed as a dependent of the target person
the other person is a member of the person's dependents
the other person is the person
both
the person is claimed as a dependent
either
			  the next person is the tax filer that claims the target person
the other person is a member of the person's tax filers
			  the next person is a member of the target's tax filer's tax household
for at least one of the person's tax filers (the tax filer)
the other person is a member of the tax filer's dependents
all
the other person is a member of the person's spouse
		    the target person and the next person are filing jointly
the other person is a member of the person's joint tax filer

the person is below the age requirement if
the person's age (for Medicaid) < 19

the person satisfies a MAGI Medicaid household exception if
the person is claimed as a dependent and
either
both
		    the target person's tax filer is not the target person's biological, adopted or step parent 		      	    From here on all types of parents are generalized to only parents
the person's tax filer is not the person's parents
the person's tax filer is not the person's spouse
all
the person is below the age requirement
the person's tax filer is the person's parents
either
both
the person lives with both parents
the person's parents are not filing jointly
the person's tax filer is the person's non-custodial parents

the person's tax filer is the person's parents if
the number of the person's tax filers > 0 and
for at least one of the person's tax filers (the tax filer)
the tax filer is a member of the person's parents

the person's tax filer is the person's non-custodial parents if
the number of the person's tax filers > 0 and
for at least one of the person's tax filers (the tax filer)

Non-Financial
Other Health Insurances Rules

[b1] the person has access to other Minimum Essential Coverage if
[b2] the person has access to public MEC or
[b3] the person has access to affordable non-public MEC

Policy Reference (HIX Final Rule): 45 CFR 155.320(b)
[b2] the person has access to public MEC if
[b4] the person attests that they have access to public MEC or
both
[b5] the person's FDSH public MEC response indicates that they have access to public MEC
[not b6] the person does not need to provide public MEC documentation

[b34] the person has insurance policies if
[InstanceCount(personsinsurancepolicies) > 0] the number of the person's insurance policies > 0

[b4] the person attests that they have access to public MEC if
[not unknown b34] it is currently known whether the person has insurance policies and
[ExistsScope(personsinsurancepolicies)] for at least one of the person's insurance policies
any
[b7] the insurance policy type is Veterans Health Insurance
[b33] the insurance policy type is Peace Corps
[b9] the insurance policy type is Medicare
 [b36] the insurance policy type is Tricare

[b5] the person's FDSH public MEC response indicates that they have access to public MEC if
[b11] the person's FDSH public MEC response verification code is yes and
[p1 >= p2] the eligibility determination date >= the person's FDSH public MEC response benefit start date and
[p1 < p3] the eligibility determination date < the person's FDSH public MEC response benefit end date

[b6] the person needs to provide public MEC documentation if
[not b4] the person does not attest that they have access to public MEC and
[b5] the person's FDSH public MEC response indicates that they have access to public MEC and
[not b12] the person's public MEC documentation has not been manually verified

the person's public MEC verification inconsistency period has not been elapsed if
the person's public MEC inconsistency notification has not been sent or
the eligibility determination date is earlier than the person's Public MEC inconsistency period end date

the person's public MEC inconsistency notification has not been sent if
the person's public MEC inconsistency notification sent date is unknown or
the person's public MEC inconsistency notification sent date is currently unknown or
the person's public MEC inconsistency notification sent date is uncertain

the person's public MEC inconsistency period end date = AddDays(the person's public MEC inconsistency notification sent date, the QHP inconsistency period)

Note: AddDays (date, number) adds the number of days to date
[b29] the person needs to provide public MEC documentation (for Medicare) if
all
[not b4] the person does not attest that they have access to public MEC
[b5] the person's FDSH public MEC response indicates that they have access to public MEC
[b32] the person's FDSH public MEC response indicates Medicare insurance policy 
[not b12] the person's public MEC documentation has not been manually verified

the person's public MEC verification inconsistency period has not been elapsed (for Medicare) if
the person's public MEC inconsistency notification has not been sent or
the eligibility determination date is earlier than the person's Public MEC inconsistency period end date (for Medicare)

the person's public MEC inconsistency period end date (for Medicare) = AddDays(the person's public MEC inconsistency notification sent date, the Medicare inconsistency period)
Note: AddDays (date, number) adds the number of days to date
Policy Reference (HIX Final Rule): 45 CFR 155.320(b)
[b3] the person has access to affordable non-public MEC if
either
[b15] the person attests that they have access to non-public MEC
both
[b22] the person's FDSH non-public MEC response indicates that they have access to non-public MEC
[not b23] the person does not need to provide non-public MEC documentation (for QHP)

4 Technical Design

4.1 Introduction
The purpose of this section is to define the technical design specifications for the functionality of Medicaid Integration.

4.2 Design

User Interface Design

Below is a listing of the user interface design directly associated with Medicaid Hierarchy. Details of the user interface technical design, describing the role played by JSPs and how pages are organized can be found in the Architecture Technical Bulletin  - RI Technical Design.

Business Layer Design

Class Diagram
This class diagram describes the component association that exists between service layer and data persistence layer. The diagram components focus on Medicaid Eligibility Process and represent the class used in Medicaid determination. Further details regarding the technical design that details the coding structure of the application and its classes can be found in the Architecture Technical Bulletin at - RI Technical Design. 


> EdUtil: 
This Class contains the Driver i.e., Entry Class for determining eligibility. This module invokes following submodule:
* EDG
* Non-Financial
* Financial
* Resource
* Verification
> EgDriver/IEgManager: 
This class is the EDG Driver, which is invoked from EdUtil. This components, determines following:
* Determines the program group composition eligibility by running OPA Group composition rules engine.
* Loads Entities
* Unloads Entities
* Passes data from Data Access Object(DAO) layer
* Runs eligibility for each month.
> NFManager:
This class is used for Non-Financial characteristics determination. This class invokes NFEntityLoader to pass data to OPA. NFEntityWriter to read data from OPA and store them in database.
> FinManager:
This class is used for Financial eligibility determination. This class invokes FinFmaEntityLoader to pass data to Financial module of the rules engine. FinFmaEntityWriter to read data from OPA and store them in database. These classes specified are used during Medicaid eligibility determination
> VCLManager: 
This class is used for Verification eligibility determination. This class invokes VCLEntityLoader to pass data to Verification module of the rules engine. VCLEntityWriter to read data from OPA and store them in database.


Exception Handling
Eligibility Application layer will throw the EDBCException when exception happens and it will be caught in Service layer. FrameworkException is used to wrap around it. Logging of exception is done at the service level. Service methods will be throwing the GenericValidationException to controller layer. Transaction manager will take care of rollback. For more details regarding the lay out the coding structure of the app and the way it traps for errors can be found in the Architecture Technical Bulletin at - RI Technical Design. 


Exception NameException Class NameRemarksEDBCExceptionus.ri.eohhs.uhip.ies.framework.exception. EDBCExceptionEDBCException  is represent the exceptions  thrown by EDBC components and the actions that could be performed when  exceptions occur.GenericValidationExceptionus.ri.eohhs.uhip.ies.framework.exception. GenericValidationExceptionGenericValidationException is used to report any exception related to the validation of Tiers data. This is used to report any server side validation and framework history validations.FrameworkExceptionus.ri.eohhs.uhip.ies.framework.exception. FrameworkExceptionFrameworkException is used by the framework to report any 
 exception that occurs during the framework process.ApplicationExceptionus.ri.eohhs.uhip.ies.framework.exception. ApplicationExceptionThis class provides a wrapper for all the application exceptions.  This is the super class for all the application level exceptions.
Caching
The Common Frameworks have provided APIs which get all the lookup data and cache it along with the APIs to get the data. Those have been used in our Reference Dao Layers to get the data used in our application and methods have been written in ReferenceServices to access the LookupData. Caching is also done at the OPA sever level.  Further details regarding the lay out of the APIs and the way lookup data is loaded to memory can be found in the Architecture Technical Bulletin at - RI Technical Design.

Further details regarding the technical design that details the coding structure of the application and its classes can be found in the Architecture Technical Bulletin at - RI Technical Design.
